The issue: When no `agentId` header is provided, the check `if (agentId && !isManager(agentId) && team.chiefOfStaffId !== agentId)` short-circuits at `agentId &&` because `agentId` is null/empty, so the 403 block is skipped entirely. This means an unauthenticated request (without agentId) can delete a closed team.  

Fix: Change the logic so that if the team is closed AND there's no agentId, return 403. The agentId must be present AND be either MANAGER or COS to delete a closed team.  

Read the file first, find the DELETE handler's closed team check, and fix the guard.

<details open>
<summary>🤖 Subagent (spark): Fix hooks CC-007 key picking</summary>

**Input:**

**Agent:** `spark` | **Description:** Fix hooks CC-007 key picking  

Fix the updateTeam optimistic update in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts  

The issue: The optimistic update at `setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: ... } : prev)` spreads ALL properties from `updates` into the team object. This could merge unexpected extra properties if the caller passes more than the expected fields.  

Fix: Instead of spreading `updates` directly, pick only the valid team update keys before spreading. The valid keys for team updates are: `name`, `description`, `type`, `agentIds`, `chiefOfStaffId`, `managerId`.  

Change the optimistic update line to explicitly pick valid keys:  
```typescript
const validKeys = ['name', 'description', 'type', 'agentIds', 'chiefOfStaffId', 'managerId'] as const
const safeUpdates = Object.fromEntries(
  Object.entries(updates).filter(([k]) => (validKeys as readonly string[]).includes(k))
)
setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...safeUpdates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)
```

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:06]*

<details open>
<summary>🤖 Subagent (spark): Fix types-lib CC-001 atomic writes</summary>

**Input:**

**Agent:** `spark` | **Description:** Fix types-lib CC-001 atomic writes  

Fix non-atomic file writes in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts  

The issue: `saveGovernance()` calls `fs.writeFileSync()` directly to the target file. If the process crashes mid-write, the file is corrupted.  

Fix: Use the standard temp-file-then-rename pattern for atomic writes:  
1. Write to a temp file in the same directory (same filesystem for rename atomicity)  
2. Use `fs.renameSync()` to atomically replace the target file  

Read the file first, find the `saveGovernance` function, and change it from:  
```typescript
fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
```
to:  
```typescript
const tmpFile = GOVERNANCE_FILE + '.tmp'
fs.writeFileSync(tmpFile, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
fs.renameSync(tmpFile, GOVERNANCE_FILE)
```

Update the comment to reflect the fix was applied (remove "Phase 2" TODO language).  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] fix-atomic-writes - <one-line result>"  
- Max 2 lines of text b  
... [19 more chars]

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-20 02:28:21]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

 Once we merge with the origin, I want you to identify from the diff all the changes introduced by the repo owner and compare them with our changes, to see if there are any incompatibilities or conflict. I'm not talking only about merge conflicts, but structural and pipeline conflicts, derived by how the design choices differs. Be sure to make first the diff and once you wrote all the changes in a document, with the help of a swarm, evaluate those changes one by one to see if there are conflicts in the program flow and design logic. Then try to make a carefully planned merge, so that it won't break our changes and fixes but it will integrate with them or in case of conflict, we need to discuss alternative solutions.  

</div>

    14→### [CC-001] Non-atomic file writes in saveGovernance risk corruption on crash  
    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts:63  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** race-condition  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** `saveGovernance()` calls `fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, ...)` directly. If the process crashes or is killed mid-write, the governance.json file can be left in a partially-written (corrupted) state. The file already has corruption detection and backup logic in `loadGovernance()` (lines 44-51), which proves this scenario is considered plausible. The standard safe pattern is write-to-temp-then-rename (atomic on POSIX).  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→  ```typescript  
    22→  // line 63  
    23→  fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    24→  ```  
    25→- **Fix:** Write to a temporary file in the same directory, then `fs.renameSync()` to the target path. This makes the write atomic. Note: this same pattern is missing in `lib/team-registry.ts:234` and `lib/transfer-registry.ts:45` (outside scope, but same issue).

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a fixed time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→// Note: check and record are not atomic — acceptable for Phase 1 single-process localhost.  
    13→// Phase 2: use atomic increment.  
    14→  
    15→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    16→export function checkRateLimit(  
    17→  key: string,  
    18→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    19→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    20→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    21→  const now = Date.now()  
    22→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    23→  
    24→  // Window expired — reset  
    25→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    26→    limits.delete(key)  
    27→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    28→  }  
    29→  
    30→  // Check if over limit  
    31→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    32→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    33→  }  
    34→  
    35→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    36→}  
    37→  
    38→/** Record a failed attempt */  
    39→export function recordFailure(key: string, windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS): void {  
    40→  let entry = limits.get(key)  
    41→  const now = Date.now()  
    42→  // Reset expired windows so stale counts are not reused  
    43→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) { entry = undefined; limits.delete(key) }  
    44→  const fresh = entry || { count: 0, resetAt: now + windowMs }  
    45→  limits.set(key, { count: fresh.count + 1, resetAt: fresh.resetAt })  
    46→}  
    47→  
    48→/** Reset rate limit on successful attempt */  
    49→export function resetRateLimit(key: string): void {  
    50→  limits.de  

... [612 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:30:27]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→/**  
    13→ * LOCK ORDERING INVARIANT:  
    14→ * When acquiring multiple locks, always acquire in this order:  
    15→ *   1. 'teams'  
    16→ *   2. 'transfers'  
    17→ *   3. 'governance'  
    18→ * Violating this order will cause deadlock.  
    19→ *  
    20→ * Current nested lock usage:  
    21→ * - transfers/[id]/resolve/route.ts: acquires 'teams' then 'transfers' (via resolveTransferRequest)  
    22→ */  
    23→  
    24→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    25→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    26→// Set of currently held lock names  
    27→const held = new Set<string>()  
    28→  
    29→/**  
    30→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    31→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    32→ */  
    33→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    34→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    35→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    36→    held.add(name)  
    37→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    38→  }  
    39→  
    40→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    41→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    42→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    43→      locks.set(name, [])  
    44→    }  
    45→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    46→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    47→    })  
    48→  })  
    49→}  
    50→  
    51→/**  
    52→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    

... [1042 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    30→/** Load governance config from disk, creating with defaults if missing */  
    31→export function loadGovernance(): GovernanceConfig {  
    32→  ensureAimaestroDir()  
    33→  if (!fs.existsSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE)) {  
    34→    // First-time initialization: write defaults and return them  
    35→    saveGovernance(DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG)  
    36→    return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
    37→  }  
    38→  try {  
    39→    const data = fs.readFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    40→    const parsed: GovernanceConfig = JSON.parse(data)  
    41→    return parsed  
    42→  } catch (error) {  
    43→    // Distinguish read errors from parse errors — parse errors indicate disk corruption  
    44→    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {  
    45→      console.error('[governance] CORRUPTION: governance.json contains invalid JSON — returning defaults. Manual inspection required:', GOVERNANCE_FILE)  
    46→      // Backup corrupted file before returning defaults to prevent silent data loss  
    47→      try {  
    48→        const backupPath = GOVERNANCE_FILE + '.corrupted.' + Date.now()  
    49→        fs.copyFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, backupPath)  
    50→        console.error(`[governance] Corrupted config backed up to ${backupPath}`)  
    51→      } catch { /* backup is best-effort */ }  
    52→      // Heal the corrupted file by writing defaults, matching the first-time init path (lines 34-36)  
    53→      saveGovernance(DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG)  
    54→    } else {  
    55→      console.error('[governance] Failed to read governance config:', error)

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:28]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix non-atomic file writes in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts  

The issue: `saveGovernance()` calls `fs.writeFileSync()` directly to the target file. If the process crashes mid-write, the file is corrupted.  

Fix: Use the standard temp-file-then-rename pattern for atomic writes:  
1. Write to a temp file in the same directory (same filesystem for rename atomicity)  
2. Use `fs.renameSync()` to atomically replace the target file  

Read the file first, find the `saveGovernance` function, and change it from:  
```typescript
fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
```
to:  
```typescript
const tmpFile = GOVERNANCE_FILE + '.tmp'
fs.writeFileSync(tmpFile, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
fs.renameSync(tmpFile, GOVERNANCE_FILE)
```

Update the comment to reflect the fix was applied (remove "Phase 2" TODO language).  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] fix-atomic-writes - <one-line result>"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:59]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `governance.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
/** Write governance config to disk */
export function saveGovernance(config: GovernanceConfig): void {
  // Fail-fast: let errors propagate to callers (all wrapped in withLock try/catch)
  ensureAimaestroDir()
  // Phase 1: non-atomic write acceptable for single-process localhost.
  // Phase 2: use temp+rename for atomicity (write to tmp file, then fs.renameSync to target).
  fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
}
```

**New:**  
```
/** Write governance config to disk using atomic temp-file-then-rename pattern */
export function saveGovernance(config: GovernanceConfig): void {
  // Fail-fast: let errors propagate to callers (all wrapped in withLock try/catch)
  ensureAimaestroDir()
  // Atomic write: write to temp file then rename to avoid corruption on crash
  const tmpFile = GOVERNANCE_FILE + '.tmp'
  fs.writeFileSync(tmpFile, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
  fs.renameSync(tmpFile, GOVERNANCE_FILE)
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX

    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `buildAMPEnvelope()` assigns `message.content.type` directly to an `AMPPayload.type` field at line 98. However, `Message.content.type` (defined in `lib/messageQueue.ts:41`) is a union of 4 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'`. Meanwhile, `AMPPayload.type` (defined in `lib/types/amp.ts:165`) is a union of 10 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'alert' | 'task' | 'status' | 'handoff' | 'ack' | 'update' | 'system'`. This means:  
    16→  1. TypeScript will NOT flag an error because the 4-value union is assignable to the 10-value union (narrower to wider).  
    17→  2. However, if an AMP message arrives via `/api/v1/route` with `type: 'task'` or `type: 'alert'` and is stored into a `Message` object, the `Message.content.type` field will contain a value that its own type definition doesn't allow. This is a silent data integrity issue -- the received AMP payload type gets silently stored in a field that claims to only accept 4 values.  
    18→- **Evidence:**  
    19→  ```typescript

    22→    type: 'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'  // 4 values

    24→  }

    26→  // lib/types/amp.ts:165

    80→ * Parse an AMP address into components  
    81→ *  
    82→ * @param address - Full AMP address (e.g., "agent@org.aimaestro.local")  
    83→ * @returns Parsed components or null if invalid  
    84→ */  
    85→export function parseAMPAddress(address: string): {  
    86→  name: string  
    87→  organization: string  
    88→  provider: string  
    89→  full: string  
    90→} | null {  
    91→  const match = address.match(/^([^@]+)@(.+)$/)  
    92→  if (!match) return null  
    93→  
    94→  // Validate name part: only alphanumeric, underscore, hyphen, dot allowed  
    95→  // Prevents spaces, control chars, path traversal sequences (e.g. "../") in agent names  
    96→  if (!/^[a-zA-Z0-9_.-]+$/.test(match[1])) return null  
    97→  
    98→  const domain = match[2]  
    99→  const dotIndex = domain.indexOf('.')  
   100→  if (dotIndex > 0) {  
   101→    // Multi-part domain (e.g., "org.aimaestro.local")  
   102→    return {  
   103→      name: match[1],  
   104→      organization: domain.substring(0, dotIndex),  
   105→      provider: domain.substring(dotIndex + 1),  
   106→      full: address,  
   107→    }  
   108→  }  
   109→

    41→  } catch (error) {

    44→  }

   316→export async function deleteTeam(id: string): Promise<boolean> {  
   317→  return withLock('teams', () => {  
   318→    const teams = loadTeams()  
   319→    const filtered = teams.filter(t => t.id !== id)  
   320→    if (filtered.length === teams.length) return false  
   321→    saveTeams(filtered)  
   322→    // Clean up orphaned task file for the deleted team  
   323→    // Defense-in-depth: validate UUID format before constructing file path to prevent path traversal  
   324→    if (/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(id)) {  
   325→      const taskFile = path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${id}.json`))  
   326→      try { if (fs.existsSync(taskFile)) fs.unlinkSync(taskFile) } catch { /* ignore */ }  
   327→      // CC-002: Also clean up orphaned document file for the deleted team  
   328→      const docsFile = path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`docs-${id}.json`))  
   329→      try { if (fs.existsSync(docsFile)) fs.unlinkSync(docsFile) } catch { /* ignore */ }  
   330→    }  
   331→    return true  
   332→  })  
   333→}

    10→### [CC-001] transfer-registry.test.ts fs mock uses named exports but governance.test.ts/team-registry.test.ts use default export -- mock style mismatch is correct but fragile  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/tests/transfer-registry.test.ts:12-22  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX (CONFIRMED -- but currently works because implementation matches)  
    13→- **Category:** api-contract  
    14→- **Description:** The `transfer-registry.ts` source uses named imports (`import { readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, existsSync } from 'fs'`), while `governance.ts` and `team-registry.ts` use default import (`import fs from 'fs'`). The transfer-registry test correctly mocks named exports (no `default` wrapper), while governance/team-registry tests correctly use the `default` wrapper. This is currently correct, but if any source file changes its import style, the corresponding test mock will silently break. **No action needed unless import style changes, but this is a documentation/awareness item.**  
    15→- **Evidence:**  
    16→  ```ts  
    17→  // transfer-registry.test.ts -- named exports (correct)  
    18→  vi.mock('fs', () => ({  
    19→    existsSync: vi.fn(...),  
    20→    readFileSync: vi.fn(...),  
    21→    writeFileSync: vi.fn(...),  
    22→  }))  
    23→  
    24→  // governance.test.ts -- default export (correct)  
    25→  vi.mock('fs', () => ({  
    26→    default: {  
    27→      existsSync: vi.fn(...),  
    28→      readFileSync: vi.fn(...),  
    29→      writeFileSync: vi.fn(...),  
    30→    },  
    31→  }))  
    32→  ```  
    33→- **Fix:** Add a comment at the top of each test file noting which import style the source uses, so reviewers can catch mismatches. No code change needed.  
    34→  
    35→**RETRACTED: On further analysis, thi  

... [22062 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:28]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix sequential COS removal in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/components/governance/RoleAssignmentDialog.tsx  

The issue: When demoting a manager (removing COS from all teams), the code uses a sequential `for...of` loop. If one removal fails partway through, some teams have been modified and some haven't, creating a partially-demoted state with no clear error reporting about which teams succeeded.  

Fix: Use `Promise.allSettled()` to attempt all removals in parallel, then check results:  

Read the file first, find the COS removal loop (around lines 169-174), and replace it with:  

```typescript
// CC-003: Use Promise.allSettled for parallel COS removal — reports partial failures clearly
const removalResults = await Promise.allSettled(
  governance.cosTeams.map(team => governance.assignCOS(team.id, null, password))
)
const failures = removalResults
  .map((r, i) => r.status === 'rejected' ? governance.cosTeams[i].name : null)
  .filter(Boolean)
if (failures.length > 0) {
  throw new Error(`Failed to remove COS from: ${failures.join(', ')}`)
}
```

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] fix-cos-removal - <one-line result>"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator  

</div>

                if (!result.success) throw new Error(result.error || `Failed for ${team.name}`)
              })
            )
            const failures = removalResults
              .map((r, i) => r.status === 'rejected' ? teamsToRemove[i].name : null)
              .filter(Boolean)
            if (failures.length > 0) {
              throw new Error(`Failed to remove COS from: ${failures.join(', ')}`)
            }
          }
        }
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/components/governance/RoleAssignmentDialog.tsx has been updated successfully.  

</details>

    72→  const handleRemoveAgent = async (targetAgentId: string) => {  
    73→    try {  
    74→      setError(null)  
    75→      const newIds = team.agentIds.filter(id => id !== targetAgentId)  
    76→      await onUpdateTeam({ agentIds: newIds })  
    77→    } catch (err) {  
    78→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to remove agent')  
    79→    }  
    80→  }  
    81→  
    82→  const handleAddAgent = async (agentId: string) => {  
    83→    try {  
    84→      setError(null)  
    85→      // CC-007: Prevent adding duplicate agent members  
    86→      if (team.agentIds.includes(agentId)) { setError('Agent is already a member'); return }  
    87→      const newIds = [...team.agentIds, agentId]  
    88→      await onUpdateTeam({ agentIds: newIds })  
    89→      setShowAddAgent(false)  
    90→    } catch (err) {  
    91→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to add agent')  
    92→    }  
    93→  }  
    94→  
    95→  return (  
    96→    <div className="p-6 max-w-3xl">  
    97→      {/* Error banner */}  
    98→      {error && (  
    99→        <div className="mb-4 flex items-center gap-2 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg bg-red-500/10 border border-red-500/20 text-sm text-red-400">

    10→### [CC-001] Stale state after AbortError in `refresh()` — `setLoading(false)` still runs  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useGovernance.ts:71,79,87,93,111-113  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** When a fetch is aborted (component unmount or agentId change), the individual `.catch()` handlers on lines 70-72, 78-80, 86-88 swallow the AbortError by returning `undefined`. The `Promise.all` resolves with `[undefined, undefined, undefined]`. The `.then()` on line 92 checks `signal?.aborted` and returns early, which is correct. However, the `.finally()` on line 111 still executes `setLoading(false)`. This calls `setLoading` on a potentially unmounted component (React 18 suppresses the warning, but in React 19+ this could throw). More critically, when `agentId` changes rapidly (e.g., user clicking through agents), this creates a race: the stale request's `.finally()` sets `loading=false` before the new request completes, causing a brief flash where `loading` is false but the data is from the old agent.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript

    21→    ...  
    22→    return { hasPassword: false, ... }  
    23→  }),  
    24→  // Line 92-93: stale guard checks signal, but...  
    25→  .then(([govData, teamsData, transfersData]) => {  
    26→    if (signal?.aborted) return  // Stale response guard  
    27→    ...  
    28→  })  
    29→  // Line 111-113: ...finally ALWAYS runs, even after abort  
    30→  .finally(() => {  
    31→    setLoading(false)  // Runs on unmounted/stale

    10→### [CC-001] document-registry: Missing path traversal protection in docsFilePath()  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/document-registry.ts:23-24  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** security  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `docsFilePath()` does not validate the `teamId` parameter. Unlike `task-registry.ts` (line 27) which validates teamId as a strict UUID pattern and uses `path.basename()` as defense-in-depth, `document-registry.ts` directly interpolates the teamId into a file path. A malicious teamId like `../../etc/passwd` would construct a path outside the intended directory.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // document-registry.ts:23-24 - NO validation  
    19→  function docsFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    20→    return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, `docs-${teamId}.json`)  
    21→  }  
    22→  
    23→  // Compare with task-registry.ts:24-29 - HAS validation  
    24→  function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    25→    if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId))  
    26→      throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    27→    return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    28→  }  
    29→  ```  
    30→- **Mitigating factor:** The API routes at `app/api/teams/[id]/documents/route.ts` call `getTeam(id)` first, which performs a lookup against the teams.json file. A malicious ID would not match any team and return 404 before `docsFilePath` is reached. However, this is defense-by-coincidence, not defense-in-depth. If any code path calls `loadDocuments()` or `saveDocuments()` directly without a prior `getTeam()` check (e.g.,

   200→    ensureTeamsDir()  
   201→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
   202→      return []  
   203→    }  
   204→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
   205→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
   206→    const teams = Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
   207→  
   208→    // Idempotent convergent migration: ensure all teams have a type field (default to 'open').  
   209→    // If two concurrent calls both trigger the migration, both produce the same result  
   210→    // (every team without a type gets 'open'), so the last write wins safely.  
   211→    // The migrationDone flag ensures we only persist the migration once per process.  
   212→    let needsSave = false  
   213→    for (const team of teams) {  
   214→      if (!team.type) {  
   215→        team.type = 'open'  
   216→        needsSave = true  
   217→      }  
   218→    }  
   219→    // CC-003: Migration write is idempotent and safe without lock — worst case is a redundant write.  
   220→    // When called from getTeam() (no lock), two concurrent migrations may both write, but produce identical output.  
   221→    if (needsSave && !migrationDone) {  
   222→      migrationDone = true  
   223→      saveTeams(teams)  
   224→    }  
   225→  
   226→    return teams  
   227→  } catch (error) {  
   228→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
   229→    return []  
   230→  }  
   231→}  
   232→  
   233→export function saveTeams(teams: Team[]): boolean {  
   234→  try {  
   235→    ensureTeamsDir()

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:28]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix the closed team DELETE bypass in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts  

The issue: When no `agentId` header is provided, the check `if (agentId && !isManager(agentId) && team.chiefOfStaffId !== agentId)` short-circuits at `agentId &&` because `agentId` is null/empty, so the 403 block is skipped entirely. This means an unauthenticated request (without agentId) can delete a closed team.  

Fix: Change the logic so that if the team is closed AND there's no agentId, return 403. The agentId must be present AND be either MANAGER or COS to delete a closed team.  

Read the file first, find the DELETE handler's closed team check, and fix the guard.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] fix-delete-guard - <one-line result>"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator  

</div>

    13→  
    14→### [CC-001] Missing UUID validation on `requestedBy` in transfers POST  
    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/governance/transfers/route.ts:52-68  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** security  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `requestedBy` field is validated for authority (`isManager`/`isChiefOfStaffAnywhere`) but never validated for UUID format via `isValidUuid()`. While the authority check effectively rejects non-existent agents (since only registered agents can hold those roles), the `requestedBy` value is stored verbatim in the transfer request on disk. A non-UUID string (e.g., path traversal attempt or very long string) would be persisted even though the authority check would fail. However, if a valid manager/COS agent has a UUID as its ID (which they do since getAgent uses UUID), this is mitigated. The inconsistency with `agentId`/`fromTeamId`/`toTeamId` (all UUID-validated) is the concern.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```typescript  
    22→// Line 62: These are validated  
    23→if (!isValidUuid(agentId) || !isValidUuid(fromTeamId) || !isValidUuid(toTeamId)) {  
    24→  return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid UUID format' }, { status: 400 })  
    25→}  
    26→// Line 68: requestedBy is NOT validated for UUID format  
    27→if (!isManager(requestedBy) && !isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(requestedBy)) {  
    28→```  
    29→- **Fix:** Add `!isValidUuid(requestedBy)` to the UUID validation check on line 62, or add a separate check before the authority verification.  
    30→  
    31→### [CC-002] Missing UUID validation on `resolvedBy` in transfers resolve POST  
    32→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maes

    }),
  },
}))
```

**New:**  
```
    copyFileSync: vi.fn((src: string, dest: string) => {
      if (src in fsStore) fsStore[dest] = fsStore[src]
      else throw new Error(`ENOENT: no such file or directory, copy '${src}'`)
    }),
    renameSync: vi.fn((oldPath: string, newPath: string) => {
      if (oldPath in fsStore) {
        fsStore[newPath] = fsStore[oldPath]
        delete fsStore[oldPath]
      } else {
        throw new Error(`ENOENT: no such file or directory, rename '${oldPath}'`)
      }
    }),
  },
}))
```

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/tests/governance.test.ts has been updated successfully.

<summary><strong>Agent `ae87d82` (unknown) [17 messages]</strong></summary>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:43]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix the updateTeam optimistic update in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts  

The issue: The optimistic update at `setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: ... } : prev)` spreads ALL properties from `updates` into the team object. This could merge unexpected extra properties if the caller passes more than the expected fields.  

Fix: Instead of spreading `updates` directly, pick only the valid team update keys before spreading. The valid keys for team updates are: `name`, `description`, `type`, `agentIds`, `chiefOfStaffId`, `managerId`.  

Change the optimistic update line to explicitly pick valid keys:  
```typescript
const validKeys = ['name', 'description', 'type', 'agentIds', 'chiefOfStaffId', 'managerId'] as const
const safeUpdates = Object.fromEntries(
  Object.entries(updates).filter(([k]) => (validKeys as readonly string[]).includes(k))
)
setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...safeUpdates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)
```

Read the file first, find the updateTeam function, and apply the fix. Update the CC-007 comment to reflect the code change.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] fix-key-picking - <one-line result>"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:35:45]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">



Let me read the file first.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 19:36:17]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `useTeam.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
    // CC-007: Optimistic update — server validates via validateTeamMutation.
    // TypeScript's excess property checking on object literals limits `updates` to declared keys,
    // but structural typing could allow extra keys at runtime; server is the authority.
    setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)
```

**New:**  
```
    // CC-007: Optimistic update — pick only valid team-update keys before spreading.
    // Structural typing could allow extra keys at runtime; explicit key filtering prevents
    // unexpected properties from polluting the team object. Server is the authority.
    const validKeys = ['name', 'description', 'type', 'agentIds', 'chiefOfStaffId', 'managerId'] as const
    const safeUpdates = Object.fromEntries(
      Object.entries(updates).filter(([k]) => (validKeys as readonly string[]).includes(k))
    )
    setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...safeUpdates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>
